311:
312:# --- I-perm-002 (#1196): semantic contraindication credit (default OFF -> literal-exact) -----
313:# The CDC contraindication source for `probiotic_immunocompromised_contraindication` says probiotics
314:# "should be avoided for patients who ... are immunocompromised" — it NEVER uses the word
315:# "contraindicated". So a FAITHFUL claim grounded in that span (e.g. drb_76 claim 03-001, "not
316:# recommended for patients who are immunocompromised", VERIFIED + cites the exact CDC url) can never
317:# contain the literal token, and the S0 `contraindications` category goes un-credited -> the safety
318:# floor reports insufficient even though the report DID warn. PG_SWEEP_SEMANTIC_CONTRAINDICATION
319:# relaxes ONLY the contraindication-CONCEPT requirement token to a curated, high-precision set of
320:# contraindication-DIRECTION phrases; the population token (e.g. "immunocompromised") is NEVER
321:# relaxed — it stays the literal precision anchor that binds substance+population (R6). A
322:# deterministic negation guard refuses credit on any opposite-direction / negated phrase so a
323:# faithful-but-INVERTED claim can never earn S0 safety credit.
324:#
325:# Direction of error is deliberate: over-crediting a contraindication is §-1.1-LETHAL (a report that
326:# wrongly believes it warned); UNDER-crediting is a SAFE disclosed gap under always-release
327:# (I-perm-001). Every layer therefore errs toward refusing credit. Four independent guards stand
328:# between a claim and S0 credit: (1) `verification.is_verified` — only strict-verified claims reach
329:# the matcher; (2) `_entity_canonical_match` — the claim must cite the entity's EXACT source;
330:# (3) the literal population anchor; (4) this negation guard.
331:_ENV_SEMANTIC_CONTRAINDICATION = "PG_SWEEP_SEMANTIC_CONTRAINDICATION"
332:_SEMANTIC_OFF_VALUES = frozenset({"", "0", "false", "no", "off"})
333:# Requirement tokens that NAME the contraindication concept — only these are relaxed to synonyms.
334:# Both singular AND plural ("contraindications") so a future config token is also relaxed (Codex P2).
335:_CONTRAINDICATION_CONCEPT_TOKENS = frozenset(
336:    {"contraindicated", "contraindication", "contraindications"}
337:)
338:# "not recommended" warns UNLESS the "recommend AGAINST" idiom inverts it ("not recommended against
339:# use" == recommended FOR use). The inverting "against" can be interposed at ANY distance ("not
340:# recommended by the CDC source against use"), so a FIXED tail window is gameable (Codex P0-3): a
341:# "not recommended" occurrence counts ONLY when NO "against" follows it anywhere in the remaining
342:# claim text (whole-tail scan). Over-refusing a warning that merely mentions "against" downstream is
343:# a SAFE under-credit. Handled separately from the imperatives below, which carry no such idiom.
344:_RECOMMEND_DIRECTIONAL_INDICATOR = "not recommended"
345:_RECOMMEND_INVERTER = "against"
346:# DIRECTIONAL IMPERATIVES — each asserts an action-prohibition for the population ("do not give this
347:# to this group"). Robustly positive: each already encodes a negation/avoidance, so inverting one in
348:# place is unnatural — presence => contraindication direction. Bare "avoid"/"unsafe"/"risk" are
349:# deliberately EXCLUDED (too easily negated / ambiguous). The bare concept stem is handled separately
350:# below (it is a noun and far easier to invert).
351:_CONTRAINDICATION_DIRECTIONAL_INDICATORS = (
352:    "should be avoided",
353:    "should not be used",
354:    "should not be given",
355:    "should not be administered",
356:    "must not be used",
357:    "must not be given",
358:    "must not be administered",
359:    "not be used in",
360:)
361:# The bare contraindication CONCEPT stem (matches "contraindicated" / "contraindication(s)"). A noun
362:# is easily negated — BEFORE it ("no known contraindications", "not generally / clearly
363:# contraindicated", "need not be contraindicated", "without contraindication") or AFTER it
364:# ("contraindications are unknown / not established / absent"). The brittle contiguous-phrase list
365:# this replaces MISSED every interposed-qualifier form (Codex P0-1: it credited "CDC reports no known
366:# contraindications ... in immunocompromised patients"). The stem counts as a positive direction
367:# ONLY when NO negation context surrounds ANY occurrence — one negated mention disqualifies the stem
368:# signal for the whole claim (conservative = SAFE under-credit, never lethal over-credit).
369:_CONTRAINDICATION_STEM = "contraindicat"
370:# Interposition between the negator and the stem (qualifier adverbs / short clauses). Tight 20-char
371:# window so a SHORT inverting qualifier ("no known", "not generally") is caught while an unrelated
372:# distant negation ("no doubt probiotics are contraindicated") is NOT — that long form stays a credit.
373:_CONTRA_NEG_INTERPOSE = r"[\w\s,'()/-]{0,20}?"
374:_CONTRAINDICATION_NEGATION_RE = re.compile(
375:    # negator BEFORE the stem (contractions are expanded to `X not` first, so `\bnot\b` covers
376:    # aren't/isn't/haven't/etc.; "free of"/"devoid of"/"zero" are short absence forms)
377:    r"\b(?:no|not|never|without|none|neither|nor|lack|lacks|lacking|few|rare|rarely|absent|zero|"
378:    r"free\s+of|devoid\s+of|unknown|unestablished|unproven|undetermined)\b"
379:    + _CONTRA_NEG_INTERPOSE + _CONTRAINDICATION_STEM
380:    # OR a negation/absence predicate AFTER the stem
381:    + r"|" + _CONTRAINDICATION_STEM + r"\w*" + _CONTRA_NEG_INTERPOSE
382:    + r"\b(?:unknown|undetermined|unestablished|not\s+(?:been\s+)?established|absent|unclear|"
383:    r"unlikely|none|negligible|rare|few)\b",
384:    re.IGNORECASE,
385:)
386:# Negative contractions -> expanded `... not` (a SPACE before "not" so the `\bnot\b` negator fires;
387:# "cannot" would join the word boundary). Apostrophe is normalized to ASCII first so a curly
388:# right-single-quote (U+2019) in scraped prose does not defeat the lookup. Expanding ALSO helps the
389:# directional route ("shouldn't be used" -> "should not be used" matches the indicator). Codex P0-2:
390:# the pre/post regex only knew expanded forms, so `aren't contraindicated` / `haven't been
391:# established` over-credited.
392:_NEGATIVE_CONTRACTIONS = {
393:    "aren't": "are not", "isn't": "is not", "wasn't": "was not", "weren't": "were not",
394:    "haven't": "have not", "hasn't": "has not", "hadn't": "had not",
395:    "don't": "do not", "doesn't": "does not", "didn't": "did not",
396:    "won't": "will not", "wouldn't": "would not", "can't": "can not", "couldn't": "could not",
397:    "shouldn't": "should not", "mustn't": "must not", "needn't": "need not",
398:    "mightn't": "might not", "shan't": "shall not", "oughtn't": "ought not",
399:}
400:
401:
402:def _expand_negative_contractions(text: str) -> str:
403:    """Normalize the curly apostrophe to ASCII, then expand negative contractions to `X not`."""
404:    text = text.replace("’", "'")
405:    for contraction, expanded in _NEGATIVE_CONTRACTIONS.items():
406:        text = text.replace(contraction, expanded)
407:    return text

410:def _semantic_contraindication_enabled() -> bool:
411:    """``PG_SWEEP_SEMANTIC_CONTRAINDICATION`` (default OFF -> literal-exact content match)."""
412:    return os.environ.get(_ENV_SEMANTIC_CONTRAINDICATION, "").strip().lower() not in _SEMANTIC_OFF_VALUES

414:
415:def _contraindication_direction_present(lowered_claim: str) -> bool:
416:    """True iff the claim asserts a contraindication DIRECTION for the population (not its negation).
417:
418:    Three independent positive routes, all fail-closed against inversion (over-crediting a
419:    contraindication is §-1.1-lethal; under-crediting is a safe disclosed gap under always-release):
420:
421:    1. "not recommended" — UNLESS an "against" follows it anywhere downstream (the "recommend
422:       against" idiom inverts it; whole-tail scan, not a gameable fixed window — Codex P0-3).
423:    2. A DIRECTIONAL IMPERATIVE ("should be avoided", "should not be used", ...) — no "against"-style
424:       in-place inverter applies, so presence => direction.
425:    3. The bare concept STEM ("contraindicat...") — only when NO negation context (pre OR post)
426:       surrounds any occurrence; a single negated mention disqualifies the stem for the whole claim.
427:
428:    Negative contractions are expanded first (`aren't` -> `are not`) so the guard is not defeated by
429:    contraction spelling (Codex P0-2).
430:    """
431:    lowered_claim = _expand_negative_contractions(lowered_claim)
432:    start = lowered_claim.find(_RECOMMEND_DIRECTIONAL_INDICATOR)
433:    while start != -1:
434:        tail = lowered_claim[start + len(_RECOMMEND_DIRECTIONAL_INDICATOR):]
435:        if _RECOMMEND_INVERTER not in tail:
436:            return True
437:        start = lowered_claim.find(_RECOMMEND_DIRECTIONAL_INDICATOR, start + 1)
438:    if any(indicator in lowered_claim for indicator in _CONTRAINDICATION_DIRECTIONAL_INDICATORS):
439:        return True
440:    if _CONTRAINDICATION_STEM in lowered_claim and not _CONTRAINDICATION_NEGATION_RE.search(
441:        lowered_claim
442:    ):
443:        return True
444:    return False

446:
447:def _content_requirements_satisfied(claim_text: str, entity: dict) -> bool:
448:    """All `coverage_content_requirements` present in the claim (case-insensitive, exact).
449:
450:    FAIL CLOSED (Codex P1): if the requirements list is empty — or somehow all-blank — return
451:    False rather than vacuously True. A bare canonical-evidence citation must NEVER earn S0
452:    credit without a real deterministic content match. (Validation in `validate_entity_severity`
453:    already blocks empty/blank S0 requirements at load; this is the matcher-side backstop.)
454:
455:    I-perm-002 (#1196): when `PG_SWEEP_SEMANTIC_CONTRAINDICATION` is ON, a requirement token that
456:    NAMES the contraindication concept ("contraindicated"/"contraindication") is satisfied by any
457:    high-precision contraindication-DIRECTION phrase (negation-guarded); every OTHER token (e.g.
458:    "immunocompromised") stays literal-exact. Default OFF -> byte-identical literal-exact match.
459:    """
460:    lowered = claim_text.lower()
461:    requirements = [
462:        token
463:        for token in entity.get(_KEY_ENTITY_CONTENT_REQS) or []
464:        if isinstance(token, str) and token.strip()
465:    ]
466:    if not requirements:
467:        return False
468:    semantic = _semantic_contraindication_enabled()
469:    for token in requirements:
470:        token_lower = token.lower()
471:        if semantic and token_lower in _CONTRAINDICATION_CONCEPT_TOKENS:
472:            if not _contraindication_direction_present(lowered):
473:                return False
474:        elif token_lower not in lowered:
475:            return False
476:    return True

479:def _claim_covers_entity(
480:    claim_evidence_records: list[Mapping[str, Any]],
481:    claim_text: str,
482:    entity: dict,
483:    *,
484:    is_s0: bool,
485:) -> bool:
486:    """Coverage test (§7.D, Codex-tightened + P2 #4).
487:
488:    ENTITY coverage: True iff the claim cites evidence whose CANONICAL identifier EXACTLY
489:    matches the entity's. anchor-string-in-sentence alone does NOT grant coverage.
490:
491:    S0 SAFETY-CATEGORY coverage (stricter): an S0 entity is covered ONLY when BOTH (a) the
492:    canonical evidence match holds AND (b) the claim text deterministically satisfies the
493:    entity's `coverage_content_requirements`. A broad source citation without the content
494:    match does NOT satisfy an S0 safety category.
495:    """
496:    if not any(_entity_canonical_match(entity, rec) for rec in claim_evidence_records):
497:        return False
498:    if is_s0 and not _content_requirements_satisfied(claim_text, entity):
499:        return False
500:    return True
501:
502:
503:# FX-03 / I-ready-017 (#1107): the 4-role seam (Sentinel decomposition + Judge) joins each
504:# EvidenceDocument.text as the SPAN the claim is checked against. Pre-FX-03 the WHOLE record text
505:# was passed, so a claim could be graded VERIFIED on support living ANYWHERE in the document, not
506:# in the cited [start:end] window (BUG-02: confirmed out-of-span false-accept, claim 06-004).
507:_GATE_B_CITED_SPAN_ENV = "PG_GATE_B_CITED_SPAN"
508:_GATE_B_SPAN_WINDOW_ENV = "PG_GATE_B_SPAN_WINDOW_BYTES"
509:_GATE_B_SPAN_WINDOW_DEFAULT = 400
510:
511:
512:def _cited_window_text(full_text: str, token: Any) -> str:
513:    """Return the cited BOUNDED-WINDOW slice of ``full_text`` for one provenance token.
514:
515:    When ``PG_GATE_B_CITED_SPAN=1`` the evidence text handed to Sentinel/Judge is sliced to a
516:    bounded window around the cited ``[start:end]`` range (±``PG_GATE_B_SPAN_WINDOW_BYTES``, default
517:    400) — the SAME tolerance strict_verify's local-window rescue uses, so the two faithfulness
518:    layers share ONE windowing policy. BOUNDED (not exact-slice) is deliberate and three-fold safer:
519:    (1) it tolerates the 06-004-shape imprecise-but-real citation that strict_verify also tolerates;
520:    (2) ``token.start/end`` index the RAW ``direct_quote`` while the record text here was
521:    ``_row_text``-STRIPPED, so an exact slice would be offset-shifted by any leading whitespace —
522:    a bounded window absorbs that small shift; (3) fail-SAFE — a degenerate/empty window falls back
523:    to the whole text so the judge is never handed a blank span. Flag off (default) returns the whole
524:    text unchanged (byte-identical), so production is opt-in per the no-silent-downgrade rule; the
525:    re-run slate activates it.
526:    """
527:    if os.getenv(_GATE_B_CITED_SPAN_ENV, "0").strip() != "1":
528:        return full_text
529:    try:
530:        start = int(getattr(token, "start"))
531:        end = int(getattr(token, "end"))
532:    except (TypeError, ValueError, AttributeError):
533:        return full_text
534:    if end <= start:
535:        return full_text
536:    try:
537:        window = int(os.getenv(_GATE_B_SPAN_WINDOW_ENV, str(_GATE_B_SPAN_WINDOW_DEFAULT)))
538:    except ValueError:
539:        window = _GATE_B_SPAN_WINDOW_DEFAULT
540:    window = max(0, window)
541:    lo = max(0, start - window)
542:    hi = min(len(full_text), end + window)
543:    sliced = full_text[lo:hi].strip()
544:    return sliced or full_text
545:
546:
547:def _resolve_evidence(
548:    tokens: list[Any], evidence_lookup: Mapping[str, Mapping[str, Any]]
549:) -> tuple[list[EvidenceDocument], list[Mapping[str, Any]]]:
550:    """Resolve each cited token -> (EvidenceDocument sliced to its cited window, source record).
551:
552:    FX-03 (#1107): one EvidenceDocument per TOKEN, carrying the bounded cited-window slice (see
553:    ``_cited_window_text``) instead of the whole record text, so Sentinel/Judge see the SPAN the
554:    decomposition prompt promises. Fail closed on an unknown id or empty record text.
555:    """
556:    documents: list[EvidenceDocument] = []
557:    records: list[Mapping[str, Any]] = []
558:    for token in tokens:
559:        evidence_id = token.evidence_id
560:        record = evidence_lookup.get(evidence_id)
561:        if record is None:
562:            raise ValueError(
563:                f"build_native_gate_b_inputs: unknown evidence_id {evidence_id!r}; every "
564:                f"cited token must resolve to an evidence record (fail-closed)."
565:            )
566:        text = str(record.get(_RECORD_TEXT_KEY) or "").strip()
567:        if not text:
568:            raise ValueError(
569:                f"build_native_gate_b_inputs: evidence_id {evidence_id!r} has empty "
570:                f"evidence text; cannot evaluate a claim against empty evidence (fail-closed)."
571:            )
572:        documents.append(
573:            EvidenceDocument(doc_id=evidence_id, text=_cited_window_text(text, token))
574:        )
575:        records.append(record)
576:    return documents, records

578:
579:def build_native_gate_b_inputs(
580:    *,
581:    multi: Any,
582:    template: dict,
583:    slug: str,
584:    domain: str,
585:    evidence_lookup: Mapping[str, Mapping[str, Any]],
586:    model_slugs: dict[str, str],
587:    d8_config: D8PolicyConfig,
588:) -> NativeGateBBundle:
589:    """Build NATIVE 4-role Gate-B inputs from a finished report + native scope contract.
590:
591:    Pure function (no I/O, no network). Returns a `NativeGateBBundle` (inputs + audit_map);
592:    M3b persists the audit map. NEVER reads `outputs/dr_benchmark/`. `domain` is carried for
593:    the audit trail / caller symmetry; the denominator comes from `template[slug]`.
594:    """
595:    entities = load_required_entities(template, slug)
596:    required_element_ids = [entity[_KEY_ENTITY_ID] for entity in entities]
597:
598:    # Validate every entity up front (fail-closed); cache (severity, s0_category) per entity.
599:    validated: list[tuple[dict, str, str | None]] = []
600:    required_s0_categories_set: set[str] = set()
601:    for entity in entities:
602:        severity, s0_category = validate_entity_severity(entity, d8_config)
603:        validated.append((entity, severity, s0_category))
604:        if s0_category is not None:
605:            required_s0_categories_set.add(s0_category)
606:
607:    claims: list[FourRoleClaim] = []
608:    audit_map: dict[str, dict] = {}
609:    for section_index, section in enumerate(multi.sections):
610:        kept = getattr(section, "kept_sentences_pre_resolve", []) or []
611:        sentence_index = -1
612:        for verification in kept:
613:            if not verification.is_verified:
614:                continue
615:            sentence_index += 1
616:            sentence = verification.sentence
617:            normalized = _normalize_sentence(sentence)
618:            digest = hashlib.sha256(normalized.encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()[:_CLAIM_HASH_HEX_LEN]
619:            claim_id = f"{section_index:02d}-{sentence_index:03d}-{digest}"
620:
621:            evidence_ids = [token.evidence_id for token in verification.tokens]
622:            # FX-03 (#1107): pass the TOKENS (carrying start/end), not just the ids — _resolve_evidence
623:            # slices each EvidenceDocument.text to the cited bounded window so the seam judges the
624:            # claim against the cited SPAN, not the whole source doc (BUG-02 out-of-span false-accept).
625:            # evidence_ids is retained above for the audit_map trail.
626:            documents, records = _resolve_evidence(verification.tokens, evidence_lookup)
627:
628:            covered_element_ids: list[str] = []
629:            covered_s0_categories: list[str] = []
630:            best_rank = _SEVERITY_RANK[_DEFAULT_OBSERVE_ONLY_SEVERITY]
631:            for entity, severity, s0_category in validated:
632:                is_s0 = severity == _SEVERITY_S0
633:                if not _claim_covers_entity(records, sentence, entity, is_s0=is_s0):
634:                    continue
635:                covered_element_ids.append(entity[_KEY_ENTITY_ID])
636:                best_rank = max(best_rank, _SEVERITY_RANK[severity])
637:                if is_s0 and s0_category is not None:
638:                    covered_s0_categories.append(s0_category)
639:
640:            claim_severity = next(
641:                sev for sev, rank in _SEVERITY_RANK.items() if rank == best_rank
642:            )
643:            s0_categories = sorted(set(covered_s0_categories))
644:
645:            claims.append(
646:                FourRoleClaim(
647:                    claim_id=claim_id,
648:                    claim_text=sentence,
649:                    evidence_documents=documents,
650:                    severity=claim_severity,
651:                    s0_categories=s0_categories,
652:                    covered_element_ids=covered_element_ids,
653:                )
654:            )
655:            audit_map[claim_id] = {
656:                "section_index": section_index,
657:                "section_title": getattr(section, "title", ""),
658:                "sentence": sentence,
659:                "evidence_ids": evidence_ids,
660:                "covered_element_ids": covered_element_ids,
661:                "severity": claim_severity,
662:                "s0_categories": s0_categories,
663:            }
664:
665:    if not claims:
666:        raise ValueError(
667:            "build_native_gate_b_inputs: zero kept (verified) sentences; a 4-role "
668:            "evaluation over no claims cannot produce a release decision (fail-closed, "
669:            "no vacuous input)."
670:        )
671:
672:    inputs = FourRoleEvaluationInputs(
673:        claims=claims,
674:        coverage_ledger=CoverageLedger(required_element_ids=required_element_ids),
675:        required_s0_categories=sorted(required_s0_categories_set),
676:        model_slugs=model_slugs,
677:        rewrite_already_attempted=False,
678:    )
679:    return NativeGateBBundle(inputs=inputs, audit_map=audit_map)

1:"""Offline replay of the D8 release policy over a SAVED run (I-perm-009).
2:
3:Reconstructs the D8 inputs from a ``SavedRun`` and replays ``apply_d8_release_policy``.
4:It REUSES the production helpers (``load_required_entities``, ``validate_entity_severity``,
5:``load_d8_policy_config``, ``apply_d8_release_policy``, AND the S0 content-requirement matcher
6:``_content_requirements_satisfied``) so there is ZERO logic drift — the harness exercises the
7:real release policy and the real S0 coverage rule, not a copy.
8:
9:Two modes:
10:
11:* ``corpus_satisfaction=False`` (BASELINE-LOCK): reconstruct coverage + S0 categories from the
12:  saved per-claim ``covered_element_ids`` / ``s0_categories`` exactly as the production run
13:  recorded them. Reproduces the saved ``held_reasons`` bit-for-bit.
14:
15:* ``corpus_satisfaction=True`` (I-perm-002 candidate): credit a required element from ANY
16:  VERIFIED claim that cites that element's evidence_id — BUT, faithful to production
17:  ``_claim_covers_entity``, an S0 SAFETY category is credited ONLY when the VERIFIED claim's
18:  text ALSO satisfies the entity's deterministic ``coverage_content_requirements``
19:  (``_content_requirements_satisfied``). This is NOT evidence_id-alone crediting (Codex A4):
20:  on drb_76 the VERIFIED Safety claims cite the contraindication evidence but their text lacks
21:  the literal required token ``contraindicated`` (they say "not recommended"/"should be
22:  avoided"), so the S0 ``contraindications`` category is NOT credited and the false hold does
23:  NOT clear. That HONEST result proves the real B2 fix needs semantic/qualitative
24:  contraindication recognition (I-perm-002) or the always-release relabel (I-perm-001), not a
25:  naive corpus-wide evidence_id credit. The R6 same-substance/risk-population guard is the
26:  production responsibility of I-perm-002.

55:_VERDICT_VERIFIED = "VERIFIED"

58:@dataclass
59:class D8ReplayResult:
60:    """Outcome of one offline D8 replay over a saved run."""
61:
62:    decision: ReleaseDecision
63:    coverage_fraction: float
64:    required_element_ids: list[str]
65:    required_s0_categories: list[str]
66:    covered_element_ids: set[str] = field(default_factory=set)
67:    credited_categories: set[str] = field(default_factory=set)

70:@dataclass
71:class _RequiredEntities:
72:    element_ids: list[str]
73:    s0_categories: list[str]
74:    s0_by_element: dict[str, str | None]
75:    entity_by_id: dict[str, dict]
76:
77:
78:def _load_required_entities(template_path: Path, slug: str) -> _RequiredEntities:
79:    """Reuse the production helpers so the required-set + S0 derivation match the real builder."""
80:    template = yaml.safe_load(template_path.read_text(encoding="utf-8"))
81:    d8_config = load_d8_policy_config()
82:    entities = load_required_entities(template, slug)
83:    element_ids = [e[_KEY_ENTITY_ID] for e in entities]
84:    entity_by_id = {e[_KEY_ENTITY_ID]: e for e in entities}
85:    s0_by_element: dict[str, str | None] = {}
86:    required_s0: set[str] = set()
87:    for entity in entities:
88:        _severity, s0_category = validate_entity_severity(entity, d8_config)
89:        s0_by_element[entity[_KEY_ENTITY_ID]] = s0_category
90:        if s0_category is not None:
91:            required_s0.add(s0_category)
92:    return _RequiredEntities(element_ids, sorted(required_s0), s0_by_element, entity_by_id)
93:
94:
95:def verified_claims_citing(run: SavedRun, evidence_id: str) -> list[str]:
96:    """Claim ids that are VERIFIED AND cite ``evidence_id`` (the per-safety-section floor input)."""
97:    out: list[str] = []
98:    for claim_id, verdict in run.final_verdicts.items():
99:        if verdict != _VERDICT_VERIFIED:
100:            continue
101:        if evidence_id in run.audit_map[claim_id].get("evidence_ids", []):
102:            out.append(claim_id)
103:    return out

105:
106:_MISSING_S0_PREFIX = "d8_s0_must_cover_missing:"
107:
108:
109:def replay_release_outcome(
110:    run: SavedRun,
111:    *,
112:    always_release: bool,
113:    template_path: Path | None = None,
114:    corpus_satisfaction: bool = False,
115:) -> ReleaseOutcome:
116:    """Replay the I-perm-001 always-release outcome (BLOCK -> LABEL) over a saved run.
117:
118:    Computes the no-fabrication hard line + the clinical safety floor from the saved verdicts:
119:    ``zero_verified`` (no VERIFIED claim), ``zero_usable_evidence`` (no cited evidence at all),
120:    ``safety_floor_insufficient`` (every required S0 SAFETY category is in the missing set).
121:
122:    ``corpus_satisfaction`` (I-perm-002 #1196): when True, the safety floor is computed from
123:    coverage RE-DERIVED through the production S0 content-requirement matcher
124:    (``_content_requirements_satisfied``) rather than the saved literal-era ``covered_element_ids``.
125:    With ``PG_SWEEP_SEMANTIC_CONTRAINDICATION`` ON this credits a faithful contraindication warning
126:    ("not recommended"/"should be avoided") that the literal-token era left un-credited — so the
127:    safety floor clears and a run that was ``released_insufficient_safety_evidence`` becomes a
128:    caveated ``released_with_disclosed_gaps``. Default False preserves the I-perm-009/I-perm-001
129:    baseline (literal-era coverage, bit-for-bit).
130:    """
131:    result = replay_d8(
132:        run, template_path=template_path, corpus_satisfaction=corpus_satisfaction
133:    )
134:    decision = result.decision
135:    zero_verified = not any(v == _VERDICT_VERIFIED for v in run.final_verdicts.values())
136:    zero_usable_evidence = not any(
137:        run.audit_map.get(cid, {}).get("evidence_ids") for cid in run.final_verdicts
138:    )
139:    missing_s0 = {
140:        reason[len(_MISSING_S0_PREFIX):]
141:        for reason in decision.held_reasons
142:        if reason.startswith(_MISSING_S0_PREFIX)
143:    }
144:    required_s0 = set(result.required_s0_categories)
145:    safety_floor_insufficient = bool(required_s0) and required_s0 <= missing_s0
146:    return compute_release_outcome(
147:        decision,
148:        zero_verified=zero_verified,
149:        zero_usable_evidence=zero_usable_evidence,
150:        safety_floor_insufficient=safety_floor_insufficient,
151:        coverage_fraction=result.coverage_fraction,
152:        always_release=always_release,
153:    )
154:
155:
156:def replay_d8(
157:    run: SavedRun,
158:    *,
159:    template_path: Path | None = None,
160:    corpus_satisfaction: bool = False,
161:    rewrite_already_attempted: bool = False,
162:) -> D8ReplayResult:
163:    """Replay the production D8 release policy over a saved run's recorded verdicts."""
164:    tpath = template_path or default_template_path()
165:    req = _load_required_entities(tpath, run.slug)
166:    required_set = set(req.element_ids)
167:
168:    credited_categories: set[str] = set()
169:    d8_rows: list[D8ClaimRow] = []
170:    covered: set[str] = set()
171:
172:    for claim_id, verdict in run.final_verdicts.items():
173:        audit_row = run.audit_map[claim_id]
174:        claim_text = str(audit_row.get("sentence", ""))
175:        s0_categories = list(audit_row.get("s0_categories", []))
176:
177:        if corpus_satisfaction and verdict == _VERDICT_VERIFIED:
178:            for evidence_id in audit_row.get("evidence_ids", []):
179:                if evidence_id not in required_set:
180:                    continue
181:                category = req.s0_by_element.get(evidence_id)
182:                if category is None:
183:                    # Non-S0 required element: canonical (evidence_id) match credits coverage,
184:                    # mirroring production _claim_covers_entity for a non-S0 entity.
185:                    covered.add(evidence_id)
186:                    continue
187:                # S0 SAFETY: credit ONLY when the claim text satisfies the deterministic
188:                # content requirements (faithful to production; no evidence_id-alone credit).
189:                entity = req.entity_by_id[evidence_id]
190:                if _content_requirements_satisfied(claim_text, entity):
191:                    covered.add(evidence_id)
192:                    if category not in s0_categories:
193:                        s0_categories.append(category)
194:                    credited_categories.add(category)
195:
196:        if verdict == _VERDICT_VERIFIED:
197:            covered.update(audit_row.get("covered_element_ids", []))
198:
199:        d8_rows.append(
200:            D8ClaimRow(
201:                claim_id=claim_id,
202:                severity=audit_row["severity"],
203:                verdict=verdict,
204:                s0_categories=s0_categories,
205:            )
206:        )
207:
208:    covered &= required_set
209:    ledger = CoverageLedger(required_element_ids=req.element_ids, covered_element_ids=covered)
210:    d8_config = load_d8_policy_config()
211:    decision = apply_d8_release_policy(
212:        d8_rows,
213:        required_s0_categories=req.s0_categories,
214:        coverage_ledger=ledger,
215:        coverage_threshold=d8_config.coverage_threshold,
216:        rewrite_already_attempted=rewrite_already_attempted,
217:        prior_fabricated_latched=run.saved_fabricated_latched,
218:    )
219:    return D8ReplayResult(
220:        decision=decision,
221:        coverage_fraction=ledger.fraction(),
222:        required_element_ids=req.element_ids,
223:        required_s0_categories=req.s0_categories,
224:        covered_element_ids=covered,
225:        credited_categories=credited_categories,
226:    )

1:"""Post-gate report.md reconciliation against the 4-role D8 verdicts (I-beatboth-fix-000 #1171).
2:
3:THE FAITHFULNESS LEAK this module closes
4:----------------------------------------
5:``scripts/run_honest_sweep_r3.py`` assembles ``report.md`` from strict_verify-KEPT
6:sentences (L5780) BEFORE the authoritative 4-role D8 seam runs (L6407+). The seam
7:re-judges every kept sentence with the stronger Mirror/Sentinel/Judge stack and can
8:flip a strict_verify-kept sentence to a non-VERIFIED verdict
9:(UNSUPPORTED / FABRICATED / UNREACHABLE / PARTIAL at ANY severity). Today the runner
10:consumes that verdict ONLY as a manifest flag (``release_allowed=False`` +
11:``needs_rewrite``); it NEVER reconciles the assembled ``report.md`` against the
12:verdicts. So a sentence the strongest verifier rejected still ships as asserted prose.
13:
14:drb_90 proof: ``needs_rewrite`` carried 7 material UNSUPPORTED claim_ids and at least
15:six of those sentences (e.g. the "$27,874 per violation" penalty figure, the
16:"UN Regulation No. 157 — ALKS" instrument line) were physically present in the shipped
17:``report.md`` body and carried-up Key Findings.
18:
19:WHAT THIS HELPER DOES (fail-closed)
20:-----------------------------------
21:For every claim whose 4-role ``final_verdict`` is non-VERIFIED, it locates the
22:claim's verbatim sentence in the rendered ``report.md`` and REPLACES it with the
23:existing visible gap language ("did not survive verification; curator-actionable gap").
24:Redaction is SEVERITY-INDEPENDENT (I-faith-003 #1174): a claim is redacted iff its verdict
25:is non-VERIFIED, at ANY severity. S3 "observe-only" governs the release LATCH only
26:(release_policy.py) — it never exempts an unverified claim from redaction.
27:
28:It is REFUSE-IN-PLACE, not a generative rewrite: no new spend, no new claims. The
29:redaction IS the "one rewrite/refuse-in-place attempt" the D8 policy docstring designs
30:but the runner never wired.
31:
32:The mapping is NOT 1:1 with strict_verify-kept (run_honest_sweep_r3.py:5660-5669 in-tree
33:caveat: downstream dedup/repair passes mutate the body). THREE TIERS of locating the prose
34:(I-redact-001 #1181 — high-recall detection, high-precision action):
35:  * TIER 1 (precise, single span): the claim's prose IS one discrete rendered sentence
36:    span (coverage >= ``_MIN_REDACTION_COVERAGE``) -> redact exactly that span, leaving
37:    every VERIFIED neighbor sentence and its [N] markers byte-for-byte (the leak fix).
38:  * TIER 2 (minimal containing unit): the claim's normalized prose is unambiguously
39:    PRESENT but it does not cover one span at the coverage floor — because a boundary
40:    under-split merged it with a VERIFIED neighbor, OR it straddles >=2 rendered spans.
41:    Redact the SMALLEST set of consecutive spans (or, only if no span set bounds it, the
42:    body line) whose concatenation contains the stem — over-redact SAFELY rather than
43:    abort (issue acceptance 1+2). The cross-line projection makes table/line-join
44:    rendering visible so this is never a silent ``already_absent``.
45:  * TIER 3 (genuinely absent): the claim's prose is genuinely ABSENT from the rendered
46:    report (downstream dedup/repair removed it) -> already not shipped; record
47:    ``already_absent`` and ship nothing extra (the SAFE state).
48:FAIL-CLOSED contract (I-redact-001 #1181): the helper RAISES ``ReportRedactionError`` ONLY
49:when a material non-VERIFIED claim's normalized prose is genuinely ABSENT from the normalized
50:report yet a real inconsistency demands a fail-closed abort — i.e. neither TIER-1 nor TIER-2
51:can bound the prose AND the prose is not cleanly absent. A merely hard-to-pin-to-one-sentence
52:claim is redacted via TIER 2, NOT aborted. The boundary hardening (``_SENTENCE_BOUNDARY_RE``,
53:I-redact-001) splits ``...risk[1] Cereal...`` / ``...adherence.[16] 87.3%...`` so the common
54:case resolves at TIER 1; TIER 2 is the defense-in-depth for any future under-split shape.
55:
56:MULTI-OCCURRENCE (I-redact-001 #1181, Codex iter-1 P1-1): the same non-VERIFIED stem can appear
57:more than once (e.g. once cleanly + once in an under-split merge). The tiered redaction LOOPS
58:per claim until the stem is absent from the line-join-normalized whole body (no occurrence left)
59:or no tier makes further progress (fail-closed) — so a second occurrence can never leak. The
60:claim is recorded in ``redacted`` exactly ONCE regardless of how many physical spans were removed.
61:
62:Pure function (string ops only; no network, no I/O). The CALLER reads/writes report.md.
63:"""

67:import re
68:from dataclasses import dataclass, field

70:# REDACTION IS SEVERITY-INDEPENDENT (I-faith-003 #1174). Any claim the 4-role seam did NOT
71:# mark VERIFIED — PARTIAL/UNSUPPORTED/FABRICATED/UNREACHABLE — must not ship as asserted prose,
72:# regardless of severity. Severity ("S0".."S3") governs the RELEASE LATCH in release_policy.py
73:# (a non-required-entity S3 claim does not BLOCK release), NEVER this redaction path: previously
74:# the S3 "observe-only" scope guard wrongly let 26 UNSUPPORTED claims (incl. clinical-safety
75:# guidance) ship across the 5 beat-both questions (BB5-F01). VERIFIED survives; every other
76:# verdict is a leak if it ships as prose.
77:_NON_VERIFIED_VERDICTS = frozenset(
78:    {"UNSUPPORTED", "FABRICATED", "UNREACHABLE", "PARTIAL"}
79:)
80:_VERDICT_VERIFIED = "VERIFIED"
81:
82:# The visible gap sentence a redacted claim is replaced with. Mirrors the existing gap
83:# language already used by contract_section_runner ("did not survive strict
84:# verification; curator-actionable gap.") so a redacted body reads consistently.
85:_GAP_REPLACEMENT = (
86:    "A claim previously stated here did not survive 4-role verification and was "
87:    "redacted; this is a curator-actionable gap."
88:)
89:
90:# gaps.json kind for a post-gate redaction (mirrors release_policy._GAP_RESIDUAL_UNSUPPORTED
91:# vocabulary but is distinct so the audit trail shows the redaction happened in report.md).
92:GAP_KIND_REDACTED_UNSUPPORTED = "redacted_unsupported"
93:
94:# POLARIS provenance token: [#ev:evidence_id:start-end].
95:_PROVENANCE_TOKEN_RE = re.compile(r"\[#ev:[^\]]+\]")
96:# Rendered numbered citation marker: [1], [12]. The final report converts each provenance
97:# token into one of these, so the stem matcher must ignore them on BOTH sides.
98:_NUMBERED_MARKER_RE = re.compile(r"\[\d+\]")
99:_WHITESPACE_RE = re.compile(r"\s+")

102:class ReportRedactionError(RuntimeError):
103:    """Raised when a material non-VERIFIED claim is present-but-unlocatable for a discrete
104:    rendered-sentence replacement. The caller MUST fail closed (do NOT ship the report).
105:    """
106:

108:@dataclass
109:class RedactedClaim:
110:    """One claim whose verbatim sentence was removed from report.md (-> gaps.json)."""
111:
112:    claim_id: str
113:    severity: str
114:    verdict: str
115:    claim_text: str  # the verbatim sentence (with its original provenance token)

118:@dataclass
119:class RedactionResult:
120:    """Outcome of reconciling report.md against the 4-role verdicts."""
121:
122:    report_text: str
123:    redacted: list[RedactedClaim] = field(default_factory=list)
124:    # Material non-VERIFIED claims whose prose was already absent from the rendered report
125:    # (downstream dedup/repair had removed them) — recorded for the audit trail, not a leak.
126:    already_absent: list[str] = field(default_factory=list)
127:
128:    @property
129:    def redacted_count(self) -> int:
130:        return len(self.redacted)
131:
132:    def gaps_json(self) -> list[dict]:
133:        """Serialize the redactions as gaps.json entries (one per removed claim)."""
134:        return [
135:            {
136:                "ref": rc.claim_id,
137:                "kind": GAP_KIND_REDACTED_UNSUPPORTED,
138:                "severity": rc.severity,
139:                "note": (
140:                    f"claim re-judged {rc.verdict} by the 4-role seam and removed from "
141:                    "report.md (refuse-in-place); curator-actionable gap"
142:                ),
143:            }
144:            for rc in self.redacted
145:        ]

148:def _prose_stem(text: str) -> str:
149:    """Strip provenance tokens + numbered citation markers, leaving the bare claim prose."""
150:    text = _PROVENANCE_TOKEN_RE.sub("", text)
151:    text = _NUMBERED_MARKER_RE.sub("", text)
152:    return text
153:
154:
155:def _normalize(text: str) -> str:
156:    """Citation-insensitive, whitespace-insensitive prose for matching across the
157:    provenance-token -> numbered-marker render shift. Trailing punctuation stripped.
158:    """
159:    text = _prose_stem(text)
160:    text = _WHITESPACE_RE.sub(" ", text)
161:    return text.strip().rstrip(".").strip()

163:
164:def reconcile_report_against_verdicts(
165:    report_text: str,
166:    final_verdicts: dict[str, str],
167:    audit_map: dict[str, dict],
168:) -> RedactionResult:
169:    """Remove every non-VERIFIED claim's verbatim sentence from ``report_text``.
170:
171:    Redaction is severity-independent (I-faith-003 #1174): a claim is redacted iff its
172:    4-role verdict is not VERIFIED, at ANY severity (S0..S3). Severity governs the release
173:    latch in release_policy.py, never this redaction path.
174:
175:    Args:
176:      report_text: the assembled report.md content.
177:      final_verdicts: claim_id -> 4-role final verdict (UNSUPPORTED/VERIFIED/...).
178:      audit_map: claim_id -> {"sentence": <verbatim>, "severity": <S0..S3>, ...}
179:                 (the persisted four_role_claim_audit.json structure).
180:
181:    Returns a RedactionResult with the redacted text + per-claim records.
182:
183:    Raises:
184:      ReportRedactionError — fail closed when a material non-VERIFIED claim's prose is
185:      present in the report but cannot be pinned to a discrete sentence to replace.
186:    """
187:    result = RedactionResult(report_text=report_text)
188:    working = report_text
189:
190:    for claim_id, verdict in sorted(final_verdicts.items()):
191:        meta = audit_map.get(claim_id)
192:        if meta is None:
193:            # A verdict with no audit row is itself a fail-closed condition: we cannot
194:            # know the claim_text to redact, and a material non-VERIFIED claim might be
195:            # shipping. Only raise for non-VERIFIED verdicts (VERIFIED never redacts).
196:            if verdict != _VERDICT_VERIFIED:
197:                raise ReportRedactionError(
198:                    f"claim {claim_id} has verdict {verdict} but no audit_map row; "
199:                    "cannot locate its sentence to reconcile (fail-closed)."
200:                )
201:            continue
202:
203:        severity = str(meta.get("severity", ""))
204:        if verdict == _VERDICT_VERIFIED:
205:            # VERIFIED survives at ANY severity. Every non-VERIFIED verdict is redacted
206:            # regardless of severity (I-faith-003 #1174): S3 "observe-only" governs the
207:            # release LATCH (release_policy.py), never this redaction path.
208:            continue
209:
210:        sentence = str(meta.get("sentence", ""))
211:        stem_norm = _normalize(sentence)
212:        if not stem_norm:
213:            # Defensive: an empty/whitespace-only claim sentence cannot be matched. A
214:            # material non-VERIFIED claim with no usable text is a fail-closed condition.
215:            raise ReportRedactionError(
216:                f"claim {claim_id} ({verdict}/{severity}) has empty claim_text; "
217:                "cannot reconcile (fail-closed)."
218:            )
219:
220:        # MULTI-OCCURRENCE LOOP (I-redact-001 #1181, Codex iter-1 P1-1): a non-VERIFIED stem can
221:        # appear MORE THAN ONCE in the body — e.g. once cleanly (TIER 1 catches it) and once in a
222:        # boundary-under-split span (only TIER 2 catches it). The prior single-pass logic marked
223:        # the claim handled after the FIRST successful removal and `continue`d, leaving the second
224:        # occurrence in result.report_text — a leak. We now loop the tiered redaction until the
225:        # stem is ABSENT from the line-join-normalized whole-body projection (no occurrence left)
226:        # OR no tier can make further progress (-> fail-closed). The loop terminates because each
227:        # successful removal replaces the matched prose with ``_GAP_REPLACEMENT`` (which cannot
228:        # re-match the stem), so occurrences are consumed monotonically.
229:        redacted_any_for_claim = False
230:        while _prose_present(working, stem_norm):
231:            # TIER 1 — precise single-span redaction (coverage floor protects VERIFIED neighbors).
232:            # One pass clears EVERY clean (pin-at-floor) occurrence across all lines at once.
233:            removed, working = _redact_sentence(working, stem_norm)
234:            if removed:
235:                redacted_any_for_claim = True
236:                continue
237:
238:            # TIER 1 made no progress this pass, but the prose IS still present (line-join
239:            # projection): it did not pin to one span at the coverage floor (a boundary
240:            # under-split merged it with a VERIFIED neighbor, OR it straddles spans). TIER 2 —
241:            # redact the minimal CONTAINING unit, over-redacting SAFELY rather than aborting a
242:            # present-but-hard-to-pin claim (#1181). TIER 2 removes ONE under-split unit per pass;
243:            # the loop re-checks presence and keeps going for any further occurrence.
244:            removed, working = _redact_minimal_containing_unit(working, stem_norm)
245:            if removed:
246:                redacted_any_for_claim = True
247:                continue
248:
249:            # FAIL-CLOSED: the prose registers as present in the line-join projection (e.g. it
250:            # spans a heading/bibliography line the redactor must not touch, or its alignment is
251:            # unbounded across non-adjacent units) but NEITHER tier could bound it to a redactable
252:            # unit without nuking a forbidden line. A real inconsistency — refuse to ship a partial
253:            # report (#1174). Raising here (not after the loop) means we never spin: no progress +
254:            # still present == abort.
255:            raise ReportRedactionError(
256:                f"claim {claim_id} ({verdict}/{severity}) prose is present in report.md "
257:                "but could not be bounded to any redactable unit (span set or body line); "
258:                "refusing to ship a partially-reconciled report (fail-closed). "
259:                f"prose_stem={stem_norm[:120]!r}"
260:            )
261:
262:        # Record the claim ONCE after the loop (Codex iter-1 P1-1: appending per removal would
263:        # double-count a claim that occurred twice and inflate redacted_count). If the loop body
264:        # never ran, the prose was genuinely ABSENT from the start — the SAFE state (TIER 3).
265:        if redacted_any_for_claim:
266:            result.redacted.append(
267:                RedactedClaim(
268:                    claim_id=claim_id,
269:                    severity=severity,
270:                    verdict=verdict,
271:                    claim_text=sentence,
272:                )
273:            )
274:        else:
275:            result.already_absent.append(claim_id)  # TIER 3 — genuinely absent, ship nothing
276:
277:    result.report_text = working
278:    return result
279:
280:
281:def _redact_sentence(report_text: str, stem_norm: str) -> tuple[bool, str]:
282:    """Replace each rendered sentence whose normalized prose contains ``stem_norm`` with the
283:    visible gap language. Returns (redacted_any, new_text).
284:
285:    Matching is done at the rendered-sentence granularity: each body line is split into
286:    sentence spans (each span KEEPS its own trailing citation markers), normalized (citation +
287:    whitespace insensitive), and a span is redacted iff its normalized prose CONTAINS the claim
288:    stem with sufficient coverage. Every NON-matching sentence — and its [N] markers — is
289:    preserved byte-for-byte, so redacting one sentence never strips citations off its VERIFIED
290:    neighbors (Codex iter-1 P1). Robust to the provenance-token -> [N] render shift; never
291:    matches across unrelated sentences.
292:    """
293:    redacted_any = False
294:    out_lines: list[str] = []
295:    for line in report_text.split("\n"):
296:        # Never touch headings, bibliography rows, or already-gap lines.
297:        stripped = line.lstrip()
298:        if stripped.startswith("#") or stripped.startswith("[") or not stripped:
299:            out_lines.append(line)
300:            continue
301:        new_line, hit = _redact_line(line, stem_norm)
302:        redacted_any = redacted_any or hit
303:        out_lines.append(new_line)
304:    return redacted_any, "\n".join(out_lines)
305:
306:
307:# A rendered-sentence boundary: a terminator [.!?], then any run of the sentence's OWN
308:# trailing citation markers ([N], optionally space-separated), then the inter-sentence
309:# whitespace, then the start of the next sentence. The trailing markers stay attached to the
310:# sentence they cite (the LEFT side) — they are NOT consumed as a separator.
311:#
312:# Codex iter-1 P1 fix: the prior `re.split(r"(?<=[.!?])(?:\[\d+\])?\s+...")` discarded the
313:# boundary marker (it was part of the matched, dropped separator), so redacting one sentence
314:# stripped the [8]/[4] citation markers off its VERIFIED neighbors on the same line and turned
315:# cited claims into uncited prose. The real drb_90 case: the VERIFIED 05-000 sentence renders
316:# "...crashes.[8]" immediately before the UNSUPPORTED 05-001 sentence — the [8] belongs to
317:# 05-000 and must survive redaction of 05-001.
318:#
319:# I-redact-001 #1181 — three ALTERNATION ARMS so a real boundary is not under-split (the
320:# under-split merged a non-VERIFIED sentence with a VERIFIED neighbor into one over-long span,
321:# dropping coverage below the floor and forcing a whole-report abort). Each arm still demands
322:# inter-sentence whitespace + a sentence-start, so decimals/abbreviations never become a split:
323:#   ARM 1 (terminator, sentence-start char): "...crashes.[8] The..." — the original behavior.
324:#   ARM 2 (terminator + >=1 marker, digit-start next): "...adherence.[16] 87.3% of..." — the
325:#          next sentence begins with a digit (defeating ARM 1's [A-Z"'(#] lookahead). REQUIRES
326:#          at least one [N] marker between the period and the digit, so a bare decimal
327:#          "0.90 (0.83 to 0.97) was found." (period, space, digit, NO marker) never matches.
328:#   ARM 3 (>=1 marker as terminator, NO preceding period): "...risk[1] Cereal...",
329:#          "...recovery[17][22] Legal..." — the renderer emitted the citation marker(s) with no
330:#          terminal period before them; the marker(s) ARE the boundary. The marker stays with
331:#          the LEFT (cited) sentence (it is m.start()-anchored, then rstrip-included in the span),
332:#          so a VERIFIED neighbor keeps its [N] byte-for-byte (the Codex iter-1 P1 invariant).
333:#          Codex iter-1 P2: ARM 3 is WORD-ANCHORED — the marker run must immediately follow a
334:#          word character ``(?<=\w)`` (NO whitespace between the sentence-final word and its
335:#          marker), so it fires only on a plausible sentence end where the renderer dropped the
336:#          terminal period ("risk[1]", "recovery[17][22]"). A MID-sentence inline citation —
337:#          "...as shown [5] In vivo..." or "the [5] Group reported..." — has WHITESPACE before
338:#          the bracket, so ``(?<=\w)`` rejects it and the inline-cited sentence stays intact (no
339:#          false split -> no over-redaction of a VERIFIED sentence). This only ever causes an
340:#          UNDER-split, which TIER 2 then bounds safely; it can never over-split a survivor.
341:# A decimal like "0.457" or "No. 157" or "U.S." is never a boundary: ARM 1/2 require whitespace
342:# before the next char and ARM 2 requires an intervening [N] marker; "U.S. products" splits only
343:# if "products" were uppercase (it is not), and "No. 157" has no marker so ARM 2 cannot fire.
344:_SENTENCE_BOUNDARY_RE = re.compile(
345:    r"(?:"
346:    r"[.!?](?:\s*\[\d+\])*\s+(?=[A-Z\"'(#])"   # ARM 1: terminator -> sentence-start char
347:    r"|[.!?](?:\s*\[\d+\])+\s+(?=\d)"           # ARM 2: terminator + marker -> digit-start
348:    r"|(?<=\w)(?:\[\d+\])+\s+(?=[A-Z\"'(#0-9])"  # ARM 3: WORD-ATTACHED marker-as-terminator, no period
349:    r")"
350:)
351:
352:# The claim stem must cover at least this fraction of a rendered sentence to redact it. Guards
353:# against a short non-VERIFIED claim whose normalized prose is a substring of a LONGER VERIFIED
354:# sentence wrongly redacting that survivor (over-redaction). Internal matching-precision floor,
355:# named per §9.4 (no magic numbers) — not an operator-tunable parameter.
356:_MIN_REDACTION_COVERAGE = 0.6
357:
358:
359:def _sentence_spans(line: str) -> list[tuple[int, int]]:
360:    """(start, end) spans over ``line``, one per rendered sentence, each span INCLUDING the
361:    sentence's trailing citation markers. The gaps between spans are pure inter-sentence
362:    whitespace, which the caller preserves verbatim — so a redaction never disturbs a
363:    neighbor's text or markers.
364:    """
365:    spans: list[tuple[int, int]] = []
366:    start = 0
367:    for m in _SENTENCE_BOUNDARY_RE.finditer(line):
368:        # m.group() == terminator + markers + trailing whitespace; the sentence (with its
369:        # markers) ends where that trailing whitespace begins.
370:        sentence_end = m.start() + len(m.group().rstrip())
371:        spans.append((start, sentence_end))
372:        start = m.end()  # next sentence begins after the inter-sentence whitespace
373:    spans.append((start, len(line)))
374:    return spans
375:
376:
377:def _sentence_matches_stem(sentence: str, stem_norm: str) -> bool:
378:    """A rendered sentence IS the rejected claim iff its normalized prose contains the claim
379:    stem AND the stem covers >= _MIN_REDACTION_COVERAGE of it (no short-substring false hit)."""
380:    sent_norm = _normalize(sentence)
381:    if not sent_norm or stem_norm not in sent_norm:
382:        return False
383:    return len(stem_norm) >= _MIN_REDACTION_COVERAGE * len(sent_norm)
384:
385:
386:def _redact_line(line: str, stem_norm: str) -> tuple[str, bool]:
387:    """Redact matching rendered sentences within a single body line, byte-preserving EVERY
388:    non-matching sentence (its exact text + citation markers) and all inter-sentence
389:    whitespace. Only the matching sentence span (including its own trailing markers) is
390:    replaced with the gap language.
391:    """
392:    # Fast reject: if the normalized line does not contain the stem, nothing to do.
393:    if stem_norm not in _normalize(line):
394:        return line, False
395:
396:    out: list[str] = []
397:    cursor = 0
398:    hit = False
399:    for (start, end) in _sentence_spans(line):
400:        out.append(line[cursor:start])  # inter-sentence whitespace, verbatim
401:        sentence = line[start:end]
402:        if _sentence_matches_stem(sentence, stem_norm):
403:            out.append(_GAP_REPLACEMENT)
404:            hit = True
405:        else:
406:            out.append(sentence)  # byte-identical — markers intact
407:        cursor = end
408:    out.append(line[cursor:])
409:    return "".join(out), hit
410:
411:
412:def _is_redactable_body_line(line: str) -> bool:
413:    """A body line the redactor is allowed to rewrite: NOT a heading (#…), a bibliography /
414:    already-gap row ([…), or blank. Mirrors the skip in ``_redact_sentence`` so TIER-2 honors
415:    the exact same no-touch set (a claim that exists ONLY inside a heading stays a fail-closed
416:    inconsistency, not a TIER-2 redaction — preserving the present-but-unlocatable contract).
417:    """
418:    stripped = line.lstrip()
419:    return bool(stripped) and not stripped.startswith("#") and not stripped.startswith("[")
420:
421:
422:def _prose_present(report_text: str, stem_norm: str) -> bool:
423:    """High-RECALL presence detector over a LINE-JOIN-NORMALIZED projection of the whole body
424:    (research practice: cross-line / table rendering is a blind spot — never silently treat a
425:    line-straddling claim as already-absent). Returns True iff the claim stem is normalized-
426:    present either within one body line OR across the join of consecutive redactable body lines.
427:
428:    Recall here only guards against a FALSE ``already_absent`` (a leak); the high-PRECISION
429:    decision of WHICH unit to remove stays in ``_redact_minimal_containing_unit`` (exact
430:    normalized containment + the coverage floor), so this projection never itself redacts.
431:    """
432:    if stem_norm in _normalize(report_text):
433:        return True
434:    # Cross-line projection: join only the redactable body lines (skip headings / bib / blanks),
435:    # normalized, and look for the stem straddling a soft line break.
436:    body = " ".join(
437:        line for line in report_text.split("\n") if _is_redactable_body_line(line)
438:    )
439:    return stem_norm in _normalize(body)
440:
441:
442:def _redact_minimal_containing_unit(report_text: str, stem_norm: str) -> tuple[bool, str]:
443:    """TIER-2 fallback (#1181): the stem is present but did NOT pin to one span at the coverage
444:    floor. Remove the SMALLEST containing unit, over-redacting SAFELY rather than aborting:
445:
446:      1. Within a single redactable body line, find the smallest set of CONSECUTIVE spans whose
447:         concatenation (normalized) contains the stem, and replace exactly that span set with one
448:         gap sentence — preserving every OTHER span (and its [N] markers) and all inter-span
449:         whitespace byte-for-byte. This handles both the boundary-under-split residue and a TRUE
450:         multi-span straddle (issue acceptance 1+2) with the same walk.
451:      2. If no within-line consecutive-span set bounds the stem (it straddles a soft line break),
452:         replace the smallest run of consecutive redactable body lines whose join contains the
453:         stem with one gap line — the coarsest safe unit.
454:
455:    Returns (redacted_any, new_text). Returns (False, unchanged) iff the stem cannot be bounded
456:    by any redactable unit (the caller then fails closed). NEVER touches a heading/bib line.
457:    """
458:    lines = report_text.split("\n")
459:
460:    # ---- 1) within-line minimal consecutive-span set -------------------------------------
461:    for idx, line in enumerate(lines):
462:        if not _is_redactable_body_line(line):
463:            continue
464:        if stem_norm not in _normalize(line):
465:            continue
466:        spans = _sentence_spans(line)
467:        span_set = _minimal_consecutive_span_set(line, spans, stem_norm)
468:        if span_set is not None:
469:            lo, hi = span_set  # inclusive span indices
470:            start = spans[lo][0]
471:            end = spans[hi][1]
472:            new_line = line[:start] + _GAP_REPLACEMENT + line[end:]
473:            lines[idx] = new_line
474:            return True, "\n".join(lines)
475:
476:    # ---- 2) cross-line: smallest consecutive redactable-body-line run --------------------
477:    redactable_idx = [i for i, ln in enumerate(lines) if _is_redactable_body_line(lines[i])]
478:    for span_len in range(1, len(redactable_idx) + 1):
479:        for offset in range(0, len(redactable_idx) - span_len + 1):
480:            window = redactable_idx[offset : offset + span_len]
481:            # The window must be CONTIGUOUS in the body-line sequence to be one rendered unit.
482:            if window[-1] - window[0] != span_len - 1:
483:                continue
484:            joined = " ".join(lines[i] for i in window)
485:            if stem_norm in _normalize(joined):
486:                first = window[0]
487:                # Replace the first line of the run with the gap; blank the remaining lines so the
488:                # leak prose is fully removed while preserving the line count (no structural churn).
489:                lines[first] = _GAP_REPLACEMENT
490:                for i in window[1:]:
491:                    lines[i] = ""
492:                return True, "\n".join(lines)
493:
494:    return False, report_text
495:
496:
497:def _minimal_consecutive_span_set(
498:    line: str, spans: list[tuple[int, int]], stem_norm: str
499:) -> tuple[int, int] | None:
500:    """Smallest (lo, hi) inclusive index window over ``spans`` whose concatenated source text is
501:    normalized-containing ``stem_norm``. Grows the window by length so the FIRST hit is minimal;
502:    prefers the smallest unit (precision: do not nuke a section when a span-pair suffices)."""
503:    n = len(spans)
504:    for window in range(1, n + 1):
505:        for lo in range(0, n - window + 1):
506:            hi = lo + window - 1
507:            seg = line[spans[lo][0] : spans[hi][1]]
508:            if stem_norm in _normalize(seg):
509:                return (lo, hi)
510:    return None
